[Programmers who care about performance often find this kind of analysis hard to swal-](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py) [low. They have a point: sometimes the coefficients and the non-leading terms make a real](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [difference.](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [Sometimes the details of the hardware, the programming language, and the](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [characteristics of the input make a big difference. And for small problems, order of growth](https://thinkpython.com/code/cartalk3.py) [is irrelevant.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubber_duck_debugging)

[But if you keep those caveats in mind, algorithmic analysis is a useful tool. At least for](https://thinkpython.com/code/pronounce.py) [large problems, the “better” algorithm is usually better, and sometimes it is](https://thinkpython.com/code/metathesis.py) [much](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [better.](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [The difference between two algorithms with the same order of growth is usually a constant](https://thinkpython.com/code/typewriter.py) factor, but the difference between a good algorithm and a bad algorithm is unbounded!

Appendix B. Analysis of Algorithms

#### [B.2](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [Analysis of basic Python operations](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[In Python, most arithmetic operations are constant time; multiplication usually takes](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spiral) longer than addition and subtraction, and division takes even longer, but these run times [don’t depend on the magnitude of the operands. Very large integers are an exception; in](https://thinkpython.com/code/grid.py) [that case the run time increases with the number of digits.](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time2_soln.py)

[Indexing operations—reading or writing elements in a sequence or dictionary—are also](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#types-set) [constant time, regardless of the size of the data structure.](https://thinkpython.com/code/emma.txt)

A for [loop that traverses a sequence or dictionary is usually linear, as long as all of the](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate.py) [operations in the body of the loop are constant time. For example, adding up the elements](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) [of a list is linear:](https://thinkpython.com/code/structshape.py)

### total = 0 [for x in t:](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann.py) [total += x](https://thinkpython.com/code/Circle.py)

[The built-in function](http://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#specialnames) [sum](http://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#specialnames) is also linear because it does the same thing, but it tends to be [faster because it is a more efficient implementation; in the language of algorithmic analysis,](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [it has a smaller leading coefficient.](https://thinkpython.com/code/has_duplicates.py)

[As a rule of thumb, if the body of a loop is in](https://thinkpython.com/code/BadKangaroo.py) [O](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [(](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [n](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal)

[a](https://thinkpython.com/code/BadKangaroo.py)

[)](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [then the whole loop is in](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [O](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [(](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [n](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal)

[a](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [+](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py)

[)](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [. The](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [exception is if you can show that the loop exits after a constant number of iterations. If a](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_frequencies) loop runs [k](https://thinkpython.com/code/most_frequent.py) [times regardless of](https://thinkpython.com/code/most_frequent.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/most_frequent.py) , then the loop is in [O](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1_soln.py) [(](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1_soln.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1_soln.py)

[a](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_frequencies)

[)](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1_soln.py) [, even for large](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1.py) [k](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1.py)

Multiplying by [k](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1_soln.py) doesn’t change the order of growth, but neither does dividing. So if the [body of a loop is in](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1.py) [O](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py) [(](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py)

[a](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py)

[)](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py) [and it runs](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py) [n](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [/](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [k](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [times, the loop is in](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [O](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [(](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [n](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e)

[a](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [+](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e)

[)](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [, even for large](https://thinkpython.com/code/birthday.py) [k](https://thinkpython.com/code/birthday.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/birthday.py)

[Most string and tuple operations are linear, except indexing and](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) len , which are constant time. The built-in functions min and max are linear. The run-time of a slice operation is [proportional to the length of the output, but independent of the size of the input.](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py)

String concatenation is linear; the run time depends on the sum of the lengths of the [operands.](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers)

All string methods are linear, but if the lengths of the strings are bounded by a constant— for example, operations on single characters—they are considered constant time. [The](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) string method [join](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) is linear; the run time depends on the total length of the strings.

Most list methods are linear, but there are some exceptions:

- [• Adding an element to the end of a list is constant time on average; when it runs](https://thinkpython.com/code/palindrome_soln.py) [out of room it occasionally gets copied to a bigger location, but the total time for](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#string-methods) n operations is O ( n [)](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [, so the average time for each operation is](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [O](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [(](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [)](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py)

- [• Removing an element from the end of a list is constant time.](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py)

- [• Sorting is](https://thinkpython.com/code/analyze_book3.py) [O](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [(](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [log](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [)](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py)

[Most dictionary operations and methods are constant time, but there are some exceptions:](https://thinkpython.com/code/cartalk3.py)

- [• The run time of](http://www.speech.cs.cmu.edu/cgi-bin/cmudict) update [is proportional to the size of the dictionary passed as a pa-](https://thinkpython.com/code/c06d) [rameter, not the dictionary being updated.](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py)

- keys [,](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [values](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [and](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [items](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [are constant time because they return iterators. But if you](https://wiki.python.org/moin/HowTo/Sorting) loop through the iterators, the loop will be linear.

#### [B.3](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1_soln.py) Analysis of search algorithms

[A](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [search](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) is an algorithm that takes a collection and a target item and determines whether the target is in the collection, often returning the index of the target.

[The simplest search algorithm is a “linear search”, which traverses the items of the collec-](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [tion in order, stopping if it finds the target. In the worst case it has to traverse the entire](http://wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby_Project) collection, so the run time is linear.

[The](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [in](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [operator for sequences uses a linear search; so do string methods like](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [find](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [and](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [count](https://thinkpython.com/code/list_exercises.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/list_exercises.py)

[If the elements of the sequence are in order, you can use a](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) [bisection search](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) [, which is](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) O ( log n ) . Bisection search is similar to the algorithm you might use to look a word up in a dictionary (a paper dictionary, not the data structure). Instead of starting at the be- [ginning and checking each item in order, you start with the item in the middle and check](https://thinkpython.com/code/palindrome_soln.py) whether the word you are looking for comes before or after. If it comes before, then you [search the first half of the sequence. Otherwise you search the second half. Either way, you](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [cut the number of remaining items in half.](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[If the sequence has 1,000,000 items, it will take about 20 steps to find the word or conclude](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py) [that it’s not there. So that’s about 50,000 times faster than a linear search.](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py)

[Bisection search can be much faster than linear search, but it requires the sequence to be in](https://thinkpython.com/code/cartalk3.py) [order, which might require extra work.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubber_duck_debugging)

[There is another data structure, called a](https://thinkpython.com/code/pronounce.py) [hashtable](https://thinkpython.com/code/pronounce.py) that is even faster—it can do a search [in constant time—and it doesn’t require the items to be sorted.](https://thinkpython.com/code/metathesis.py) [Python dictionaries are](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [implemented using hashtables, which is why most dictionary operations, including the](https://thinkpython.com/code/typewriter.py) [in](https://thinkpython.com/code/interlock.py) operator, are constant time.

Appendix B. Analysis of Algorithms

#### [B.4](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [Hashtables](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[To explain how hashtables work and why their performance is so good, I start with a simple](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [implementation of a map and gradually improve it until it’s a hashtable.](https://thinkpython.com/code/spiral.py)

[I use Python to demonstrate these implementations, but in real life you wouldn’t write](https://thinkpython.com/code) [code like this in Python; you would just use a dictionary! So for the rest of this chapter, you](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time2_soln.py) [have to imagine that dictionaries don’t exist and you want to implement a data structure](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#types-set) that maps from keys to values. The operations you have to implement are:

add(k, v) [:](https://thinkpython.com/code/pi.py) [Add a new item that maps from key](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) [k](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) [to value](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) [v](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) . With a Python dictionary, d , [this operation is written](https://thinkpython.com/code/structshape.py) [d[k] = v](https://thinkpython.com/code/structshape.py) [.](https://thinkpython.com/code/structshape.py)

get(k) : Look up and return the value that corresponds to key [k](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [. With a Python dictionary,](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann.py) [d](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [, this operation is written](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann.py) d[k] or d.get(k) .

For now, I assume that each key only appears once. The simplest implementation of this [interface uses a list of tuples, where each tuple is a key-value pair.](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e)

```
class LinearMap:
```

### [def __init__(self):](https://thinkpython.com/code/draw.py) [self.items = []](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_frequencies)

### [def add(self, k, v):](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1_soln.py) [self.items.append((k, v))](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py)

### [def get(self, k):](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [for key, val in self.items:](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation) [if key == k:](https://thinkpython.com/code/wordlist.py) return val [raise KeyError](https://thinkpython.com/code/reducible.py)

add appends a key-value tuple to the list of items, which takes constant time.

[get](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) [uses a](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) [for](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) [loop to search the list: if it finds the target key it returns the corresponding](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) [value; otherwise it raises a](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) KeyError . So get is linear.

An alternative is to keep the list sorted by key. Then get could use a bisection search, which is O ( log n ) . But inserting a new item in the middle of a list is linear, so this might not be the best option. There are other data structures that can implement add [and](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#string-methods) [get](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#string-methods) [in log time,](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#string-methods) [but that’s still not as good as constant time, so let’s move on.](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py)

[One way to improve](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [LinearMap](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [is to break the list of key-value pairs into smaller lists.](http://gutenberg.org/) Here’s an implementation called [BetterMap](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py) [, which is a list of 100 LinearMaps. As we’ll](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py) [see in a second, the order of growth for](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [get](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [is still linear, but](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) BetterMap [is a step on the](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [path toward hashtables:](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number)

```
class BetterMap:
```

### [def __init__(self, n=100):](https://thinkpython.com/code/pronounce.py) [self.maps = []](https://thinkpython.com/code/double.py) [for i in range(n):](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) self.maps.append(LinearMap())

B.4. Hashtables

### def find_map(self, k): [index = hash(k) % len(self.maps)](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [return self.maps[index]](https://thinkpython.com/code/spiral.py)

### def add(self, k, v): m = self.find_map(k) [m.add(k, v)](http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/3.0/)

### [def get(self, k):](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate.py) [m = self.find_map(k)](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function) [return m.get(k)](https://thinkpython.com/code/structshape.py)

__init__ makes a list of n LinearMap s.

find_map is used by add and get to figure out which map to put the new item in, or which [map to search.](https://thinkpython.com/code/Circle.py)

[find_map](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birthday_paradox) [uses the built-in function](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [hash](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) , which takes almost any Python object and returns [an integer. A limitation of this implementation is that it only works with hashable keys.](https://thinkpython.com/code/has_duplicates.py) Mutable types like lists and dictionaries are unhashable.

[Hashable objects that are considered equivalent return the same hash value, but the con-](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_frequencies) [verse is not necessarily true: two objects with different values can return the same hash](https://thinkpython.com/code/Time1_soln.py) [value.](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate_pairs.py)

[find_map](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [uses the modulus operator to wrap the hash values into the range from 0 to](https://thinkpython.com/code/do_four.py) [len(self.maps)](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) , so the result is a legal index into the list. Of course, this means that many different hash values will wrap onto the same index. But if the hash function spreads things [out pretty evenly (which is what hash functions are designed to do), then we expect](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [/100](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [items per LinearMap.](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[Since the run time of](https://thinkpython.com/code/reducible.py) [LinearMap.get](https://thinkpython.com/code/reducible.py) is proportional to the number of items, we expect [BetterMap to be about 100 times faster than LinearMap. The order of growth is still linear,](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [but the leading coefficient is smaller. That’s nice, but still not as good as a hashtable.](https://thinkpython.com/code/words.txt)

[Here (finally) is the crucial idea that makes hashtables fast: if you can keep the maximum](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) length of the LinearMaps bounded, LinearMap.get is constant time. All you have to do is keep track of the number of items and when the number of items per LinearMap exceeds a threshold, resize the hashtable by adding more LinearMaps.

[Here is an implementation of a hashtable:](http://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#string-methods)

```
class HashMap:
```

### [def __init__(self):](https://thinkpython.com/code/koch.py) [self.maps = BetterMap(2)](https://thinkpython.com/code/pie.py) [self.num = 0](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_snowflake)

### def get(self, k): [return self.maps.get(k)](https://thinkpython.com/code/pronounce.py)

[def add(self, k, v):](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) if self.num == len(self.maps.maps):

Appendix B. Analysis of Algorithms

### [self.resize()](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

### [self.maps.add(k, v)](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [self.num += 1](https://thinkpython.com/code/spiral.py)

### def resize(self): new_maps = BetterMap(self.num * 2)

### [for m in self.maps.maps:](https://thinkpython.com/code/emma.txt) [for k, v in m.items:](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate.py) [new_maps.add(k, v)](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ackermann_function)

### [self.maps = new_maps](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann_memo.py)

[__init__](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [creates a](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann.py) [BetterMap](https://thinkpython.com/code/ackermann.py) and initializes num , which keeps track of the number of items.

| of items and the size of the | BetterMap | : if they are equal, the average number of items per |
| ---------------------------- | --------- | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| LinearMap is 1, so it calls  | resize    | .                                                    |

resize [makes a new](https://thinkpython.com/code/Map.py) BetterMap [, twice as big as the previous one, and then “rehashes” the](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [items from the old map to the new.](https://thinkpython.com/code/draw.py)

Rehashing is necessary because changing the number of LinearMaps changes the denomi- [nator of the modulus operator in](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate_pairs.py) [find_map](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate_pairs.py) [. That means that some objects that used to hash](https://thinkpython.com/code/Point1_soln.py) [into the same LinearMap will get split up (which is what we wanted, right?).](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e)

[Rehashing is linear, so](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) [resize](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) is linear, which might seem bad, since I promised that add would be constant time. But remember that we don’t have to resize every time, so [add](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation) [is](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation) [usually constant time and only occasionally linear. The total amount of work to run](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [add](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [times is proportional to](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/wordlist.py) [, so the average time of each](http://wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby_Project) [add](http://wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby_Project) [is constant time!](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[To see how this works, think about starting with an empty HashTable and adding a se-](https://thinkpython.com/code/reducible.py) [quence of items. We start with 2 LinearMaps, so the first 2 adds are fast (no resizing re-](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) quired). Let’s say that they take one unit of work each. The next add requires a resize, so [we have to rehash the first two items (let’s call that 2 more units of work) and then add the](http://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html) third item (one more unit). Adding the next item costs 1 unit, so the total so far is 6 units of work for 4 items.

The next add costs 5 units, but the next three are only one unit each, so the total is 14 units for the first 8 adds.

The next add [costs 9 units, but then we can add 7 more before the next resize, so the total is](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py) [30 units for the first 16 adds.](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py)

[After 32 adds, the total cost is 62 units, and I hope you are starting to see a pattern. After](https://docs.python.org/3/library/pdb.html) [n](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) adds, where [n](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [is a power of two, the total cost is 2](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci_number) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/analyze_book3.py) [−](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [2 units, so the average work per add](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_snowflake) [is a little less than 2 units. When](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_snowflake) [n](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_snowflake) [is a power of two, that’s the best case; for other values of](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [the average work is a little higher, but that’s not important. The important thing is that it](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubber_duck_debugging) is O ( ) .

[Figure B.1 shows how this works graphically. Each block represents a unit of work. The](https://thinkpython.com/code/metathesis.py) [columns show the total work for each add in order from left to right: the first two](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [adds](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_db.py) [cost](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_db.py) 1 unit each, the third costs 3 units, etc.

B.5. Glossary

[Figure B.1: The cost of a hashtable add.](https://thinkpython.com/code/rotate.py)

[The extra work of rehashing appears as a sequence of increasingly tall towers with increas-](http://www.thinkpython.com/) [ing space between them. Now if you knock over the towers, spreading the cost of resizing](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) over all adds, you can see graphically that the total cost after n adds is 2 n − 2.

[An important feature of this algorithm is that when we resize the HashTable it grows](http://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#specialnames) [geometrically;](http://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#specialnames) [that is, we multiply the size by a constant.](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) If you increase the size [arithmetically—adding a fixed number each time—the average time per](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birthday_paradox) add is linear.

You can download my implementation of HashMap from [https://thinkpython.com/](https://thinkpython.com/code/markov.py) [code/Map.py](https://thinkpython.com/code/draw.py) [, but remember that there is no reason to use it; if you want a map, just use a](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexagesimal) [Python dictionary.](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_frequencies)

#### [B.5](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) Glossary

[analysis of algorithms:](http://tinyurl.com/thinkpython2e) A way to compare algorithms in terms of their run time and/or [space requirements.](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation)

[machine model:](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [A simplified representation of a computer used to describe algorithms.](http://wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby_Project)

[worst case:](http://www.cartalk.com/content/puzzlers) [The input that makes a given algorithm run slowest (or require the most](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py) [space).](https://thinkpython.com/code/PokerHandSoln.py)

leading term: In a polynomial, the term with the highest exponent.

[crossover point:](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix_sort) The problem size where two algorithms require the same run time or space.

order of growth: [A set of functions that all grow in a way considered equivalent for pur-](https://thinkpython.com/code/palindrome_soln.py) poses of analysis of algorithms. For example, all functions that grow linearly belong [to the same order of growth.](https://thinkpython.com/code/flower.py)

Big-Oh notation: [Notation for representing an order of growth; for example,](http://gutenberg.org/) [O](https://thinkpython.com/code/sed.py) [(](https://thinkpython.com/code/sed.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/sed.py) [)](https://thinkpython.com/code/sed.py) [repre-](https://thinkpython.com/code/sed.py) [sents the set of functions that grow linearly.](https://docs.python.org/3/library/pdb.html)

[linear:](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [An algorithm whose run time is proportional to problem size, at least for large](https://thinkpython.com/code/anagram_sets.py) [problem sizes.](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_snowflake)

[quadratic:](http://www.speech.cs.cmu.edu/cgi-bin/cmudict) [An algorithm whose run time is proportional to](https://thinkpython.com/code/c06d) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py) [, where](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py) [n](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py) [is a measure of](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py) [problem size.](https://thinkpython.com/code/reverse_pair.py)

[search:](http://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators) [The problem of locating an element of a collection (like a list or dictionary) or](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collatz_conjecture) determining that it is not present.

Appendix B. Analysis of Algorithms

[hashtable:](https://thinkpython.com/code/polygon.py) [A data structure that represents a collection of key-value pairs and performs](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zipf's_law) search in constant time.
